text:
This recipe was wonderful! I made some changes to the original recipe, varying only slightly. I substituted shredded butternut squash in place of the carrot, and I curried my lentils before adding them with the broth. The curried flavor really carried over well through out the simmering, and the texture was really nice when I used an immersion blender on the whole soup to get everything blended very fine. Overall, I prefer to blend everything rather than leave parts of it chunky. Thank you for the recipe!

text:
I reduced the olive oil to 1 TB, for sauteing the onions and garlic (which I upped to 4 cloves because I love garlic and some other reviewers complained of blandness), because for health reasons I need to avoid fats and oils as much as possible. I omitted the final 4 tsp of olive oil added at the end entirely. And despite that, this was delicious! So anyone who needs to reduce their fat intake can feel safe reducing the oil called for in the recipe, without fear of ruining the recipe.

I made this as written. It is so simple and flavorful. I live in the Detroit area, surrounded by places to get Middle Eastern and Indian food. My husband and I eat both often. text:
This was the first recipe that I used for cooking lentils for the first time and it was great!!!  I highly recommend this recipe.  The only changes I made was only due to lack of ingredients at home and I didn't want to go out and buy more ingredients.  I substituted the 1 tablespoon of tomato paste with 4 tablespoons of crushed tomatoes, replaced the chicken broth with boullion cubes with water therefore reducing the salt to less than 1/4 tsp.  I used 1 1/2 cups of green lentils.  I used a pressure cooker and cooked it on high to the second ring and let it naturally release until it reached the first ring and then quick released the pressure.  If you have a pressure cooker, I would definitely recommend using it since it will cut the cooking time down tremendously.

I love lentil soup and this recipe didn't disappoint.  Easy and quick to put together with little need for a shopping list.  

I agree that the portions are small and made the following adjustments:

1) added a 14oz additional can of chicken broth  
 stretch it some 2) added more spice "to taste".  3) I also did not blend any portion of the soup and left it chunky/broth style 4) used the juice of an entire lemon (could have used more) 5) used 2 carrots.

Easy breezy recipe with great flavors.  What a great addition to the recipe box!

This recipe is a keeper. It has a wonderful flavor. I couldn't find red lentils on my only stop so used brown lentils that I soaked for an hour before starting the soup. I stick to 1/3 of the container just to be safe.)

This was phenomenal! I taste tested it after it had been simmering about 30 minutes and some of the lentils were still firm, so I simmered another 10 minutes before testing again.  At that point I went ahead and added the lemon juice, saving the cilantro as a garnish as some in my family don't care for it. This is one of the best soups I've ever tasted!

text:
This is an excellent recipe.  I'm leaving a review because I had to use brown lentils and it changed the cooking instructions.  I prepared everything as directed but with one cup of brown lentils instead of red.  I had to simmer the lentils for an additional 25 minutes, bringing the total cooking time to 55 minutes.  I put the entire batch in the blender and pulsed a few times until it was smooth but still a little chunky.  I then returned the soup to the pot and added one cup of hot water along with the lemon juice.  The finished soup came out very thick and wonderful but it only made two dinner-sized servings.  Next time I will quadruple the recipe.

text:
This is delicious!  I had to make a few alterations because I didn't have everything.  I used one tamarillo (tree tomato) instead of tomato paste, veggie broth instead of chicken, one sweet potato instead of a carrot, and I didn't use cilantro or oil to drizzle or the pinch of chili powder, plus I used a little less broth than called for. First I sauted the onion for a few minutes, then I added the sweet potato.  After about five minutes I added the garlic and spices and sauted for another three or so minutes. Finally I added the broth and put a cover on it.  It cooked a lot faster than 30 minutes, probably only 20 and everything was cooked enough to eat.  I decided to pureed it all instead of leaving it chunky.  In the bowl I put a squeeze of fresh lemon juice on top. We were both very pleased with the result. I will definitely make this again!

Amazing how simple ingredients can come together and make such a complete healthy and satisfying meal. I love lemon and I'm crazy about cilantro, so I added probably double what the recipe called for. Make sure you add salt last, if not your lentils will be hard, so it's good that it's included in the recipe. Very tasty!  For us it's better as a chowder or side dish.

We made the following changes:  saute onion, garlic and carrots over medium until very tender.  Add about 1/4 tsp. curry with spices and use marinara instead of tomato paste.  Only use 3 cups chicken broth so it's a bit thicker rather than soup-like. No olive oil or extra chili powder to finish just cilantro & lime juice.  

N - with sour cream
C - with grilled chicken and naan.

text:
This is my go-to soup! I use ketchup whenever I make it so I don't have to buy tomato paste. I use vegetable broth because I'm vegetarian. And I skip the olive oil drizzle and chili powder at the end; I don't find that it needs it. Very minimal changes that I doubt change the flavor very much at all. I find that it takes less than 45 minutes to make, and it's a piece of cake to make since 30 of those minutes it's just simmering! I use an immersion blender at the end to get it to a consistency I like. My boyfriend and I gobble this up every time!!

text:
What a great recipe!  It's not often that I find one that I don't have to alter at all.  I did make a few additions, based on taste and what I had available.  I used a can of original Ro-Tel instead of tomato paste and cumin, which gave the soup a nice kick.  I also pureed the onion/garlic/tomato/carrot mixture after it had cooked and before I added the chicken broth and lentils.  Then instead of pureeing the lentils, I added a can of pureed black beans for body.  What a hit!!

text:
Let me just say first that i realize this review isn't entirely fair...  When i try a new recipe, i try to stay with how the author intended it to be - just for the first time and then i tweek it after.  So, i stayed true to the recipe and it was good but i just couldn't get past the chicken broth (i'm a vegetarian but can on occassion deal with meat broth - not in this case, unfortunately).  So, i decided to try again and use vegetable broth instead.  Also, i tried a masala mix i had instead of the cumin and LOVED this!  That's why i gave it 4 stars instead of 5 because, chicken broth aside, i much preferred it with the mixed spice blend than just the cumin.  Overall, really wonderful and will be adding this to my list of favorites - my 3 year old even loved it!

this soup was REALLY tasty.  I pretty much followed the recipe other than adding about a stalk of diced celery  after sauting the onion and before adding the liquid.  I also used a bit more broth and did not add salt until the end-- to taste. I used the immersion blender (much easier/cleaner) .  The lemon adds great flavor and do not skip that step.  I've made lots of lentil soups and they were all decent, not great.  I would call this one the exception to that rule.

text:
Ive made this several times and it never disappoints. Its delicious! I made a couple changes to the original recipe. I use 2 Tbsp. Olive oil to saut the onions and garlic. I usually use green lentils because I cant find the red ones. I use the exact spices and their measurements and use the tomato paste in the squeeze tube so you dont waste the rest of the can. For the vegetables, I usually add an extra carrot, a stalk of celery, and sometimes a sweet potato. Ive made it where Ive pured half and also when I havent pured at all. Sometimes I forget the cilantro on top and dont use the extra olive oil either. I usually put a spoonful of Greek yogurt on top. This is the ONLY recipe for lentil soup I will use now and Ive been making lentil soup for years experimenting with other recipes.

text:
I have made this soup several times, it's delicious. Excellent recipe. The first time, I made it exactly as written. It is excellent as is. The next couple of times I changed some things up to personal taste, (as cooks do) for anyone that's interested in that:
 I used 1/2 coconut oil 1/2 olive oil to start.
 I add either a head of chopped kale or spinach between steps 1 & 2.
I double all the spices.  
At the end with the cilantro & lemon juice, I add 2 cloves minced garlic.  
Next time I think I will add a dash turmeric, dash cinnamon,  dash coriander.  
For anyone that can't do cilantro (my Dad can't), the cilantro here is key, but if I had to sub., I would try parsley or perhaps Thai basil. 
Thank s for the wonderful recipe!

I tweaked it to my own taste by adding a pinch of curry with the cumin and chili seasoning. Salt and pepper. I did not have tomato paste so I added maybe 2 tablespoons of thick tomato sauce (from the small Goya can).  I probably added 3 cloves of garlic (minced from the jar).  Used Vegetable Stock. I omitted the lemon and cilantro because I wasn't in the mood for those flavors.  Really liked it.  Will make again.

I made this as it's written.  After I tried a bit, I believed it was just great but a little...empty?  So I put dashes of cayenne, cinnamon, cardamon and ginger.  Per the recipe, adding the fresh squeezed lemon juice, olive oil and cilantro completed this lovely soup.   I tripled the recipe in hopes of having enough for a family of 12. Thankfully there will be other food but it looks like a lot of soup.  This is a fantastic recipe!  Next time I will add a few more veggies to make it even heartier, like cabbage, celery and cauliflower, mostly because it would be easy to hide these in this soup for people who won't eat them normally!  Yippee!!  (I gave it four stars because I did add a few more ingredients. I used chicken bone broth and added additional salt as well.)

text:
Yummy! I recently had red lentil soup at a local Mediterranean restaurant and absolutely loved it. So, I wanted to find a replica recipe I could make right at home -- without having to pay to go out to get it and THIS is definitely it!  It was just right, without being overpowering in flavor. I didn't follow the pureeing the recipe recommended, only because we're in temporary housing and I don't have a blender at my disposal. However, when I get my kitchen back, I will definitely be pureeing the broth, garlic, and onions before adding the lintels and carrot. Also, I will be pureeing half the soup after lintels and carrots are made as suggested, which will help with thickness and cut back on it being too chunky. Because, it is. The only adjustment I might make to the recipe itself is to omit the lemon juice again (as I did this time) add a touch more cumin, as tasted just right, but needs just a touch more flavor. To add more, I will also let the lentils cook at least 45 minutes to an hour next time. They were fine, but I like mine to be a little more soft. Will be making again and serving with hot naan bread to compliment!

text:
This recipe is very similar to the recipe on the bag of red lentils that I bought at the local halal market. I doubled it and used my own homemade chicken bone broth. If you use homemade broth, it needs more salt than is called for in the recipe, but if you're using store bought broth (which is what it calls for), then it probably doesn't.  With the recipe doubled, I used the juice of a whole lemon and in place of fresh cilantro, I used dried. I liked the serving suggestion of sprinkling chili powder over the individual bowls, but with bone broth, it does NOT need a drizzle of olive oil.  I'm sure that if you use the boxed broth, it would really benefit from it though. Instead of transferring half the soup to a blender, I just used my immersion blender right in the pot, and only ran it a couple of times to keep it slightly chunky. It was perfect. My family loved this, and I will definitely be making it again.

text:
I have made this recipe several times, always doubling it, and it's excellent every time - a big hit with guests.  I've tinkered with the spices a bit (usually adding a pinch of celery salt and a pinch of cayenne, and some granulated garlic) too, but if you want to take this recipe to a whole new level, forget about the olive oil drizzle.  There's an amazing oil from Morocco that's becoming more available called ARGON OIL!  It has culinary and other qualities that border on amazing!  Gourmet stores might have it, or you can order it online.  It turns this soup recipe into something you'll never forget.

text:
Im trying to eat more vegetarian meals and learned that lentils are a good source of protein.  Came across this recipe thinking it would be good for my work lunches but not so much as a family dinner.  So wrong!  When making it one afternoon the family smelled the aroma and swarmed the kitchen.   After a taste test by all they decided they wanted it for dinner instead of what I already planned.  Served it with naan and everyone loved it.    

To make the meal go further I added extra carrots and a few small Yukon gold potatoes.  Also added curry powder and hot Indian chili power in place of the regular chili power.   Next time I will double the recipe to fill up a family of 3 and to have enough leftover for my work lunches.   Definitely a keeper to add to the weeknight meal rotation.

text:
My first time cooking lentils. This recipe is a great starting-off point. We don't buy chicken stock, just use Better than Buillion and adjust the salt. I doubled everything except the onion and added celery, kale and fresh ginger. I had a "curry spice" from Trader Joe's, which had cumin, ginger, nutmeg, onion, garlic and chili - I put about a tsp of that, also. I messed with it, added more water, kept tasting, kept messing with it, and the soup adjusted amazingly. I added a tsp or two of sea salt towards the end, with more spices in a bit of water. This recipe is pretty hard to mess up. The lentils cooked down to pretty much mush by the time it finished absorbing the water (as in, the leftovers), but it's just as amazing regardless. 
Tried this a second time with chicken stock (regular sodium, since my husband will avoid food without salt). Left out the kale and added ground chicken basil sausage. Didn't need the lemon because I tossed in some whole ginger and let it simmer. Had to add cinnamon to cut the tart of the ginger flavor. Skipped the cilantro and tomato. Oh yum. I think I officially declare now that lentil soup is the best soup I make.

I thought this was good lentil soup. So super easy to make and with stuff I normally have in the house, for the most part. It all fit in a 3" lidded pot, making clean-up easy too. I followed the recipe exactly, just with the spices I did one pinch of them all and 2 pinches of cumin. I find most spices to be in over-powering amounts in many recipes. It does only make 4 servings, as suggested, but is fine for lunch or a quick last minute supper with bread or something similar.

text:
after reading many reviews and other recipes I wanted to make sure my soup had enough flavor and here is what I did.  I think the soup came out really good and will make it again.

use 1 1/2 cups lentils, used lots of garlic than suggested at least 8 mediums size cloves, at least a cup of carrots, 2 sticks of celery, added some garden riped tomatoes, used 2 - 3 tsp of cumin, doubles the chili powder, used ketchup instead of paste, tripled the broth ( mixed beef & chicken b/c I had it open) added a big squirt or 2 of siracha sauce, added 1 potatoe chunked big.  I also added fresh baby spinach and broken spaghetti that I cooked separate.  I did keep adding chicken broth as it was cooking to avoid all beans an no broth.  I did puree some of the beans a potatoes for texture.  The lemon and red wine vinegar do bring out the flavors in the soup.

Very yummy! blending only half the soup really gave it a perfect texture. I will remeber that in the future when making any lentil soup. The cilantro added a really fresh flavor but I would suggest not adding it until the very last minute so that the flavor doesn't get cooked in too throughly. I added some additions that made it very flavorful and quite good. I added gharam masala, cumin and turmeric. It might be too much flavor for some tastes, but I thought it was just right.
